   991	/* Return the pointer to the cluster node that is able to serve the command.
   992	 *
   993	 * Note that this function doesn't compute the slot for each key. The client's
   994	 * slot needs to be set before calling this function. If it's set to -1, the
   995	 * client's read flags should indicate if it's a cross-slot command or if the
   996	 * command has no keys. This is computed by clusterSlotByCommand(). The commands
   997	 * can be called together like this:
   998	 *
   999	 *     c->slot = clusterSlotByCommand(c->cmd, c->argv, c->argc, &c->read_flags);
  1000	 *     node = getNodeByQuery(c, &error_code);
  1001	 *
  1002	 * For the function to succeed the command should only target either:
  1003	 *
  1004	 * 1) A single key (even multiple times like RPOPLPUSH mylist mylist).
  1005	 * 2) Multiple keys in the same hash slot, while the slot is stable (no
  1006	 *    resharding in progress).
  1007	 *
  1008	 * The EXEC command is a special case. It takes no keys so the slot for this
  1009	 * command is -1, but this function updates the client's slot to be the slot of
  1010	 * the complete MULTI-EXEC transaction.
  1011	 *
  1012	 * On success the function returns the node that is able to serve the request.
  1013	 * If the node is not 'myself' a redirection must be performed. The kind of
  1014	 * redirection is specified setting the integer passed by reference
  1015	 * 'error_code', which will be set to CLUSTER_REDIR_ASK or
  1016	 * CLUSTER_REDIR_MOVED.
  1017	 *
  1018	 * When the node is 'myself' 'error_code' is set to CLUSTER_REDIR_NONE.
  1019	 *
  1020	 * If the command fails NULL is returned, and the reason of the failure is
  1021	 * provided via 'error_code', which will be set to:
  1022	 *
  1023	 * CLUSTER_REDIR_CROSS_SLOT if the request contains multiple keys that
  1024	 * don't belong to the same hash slot.
  1025	 *
  1026	 * CLUSTER_REDIR_UNSTABLE if the request contains multiple keys
  1027	 * belonging to the same slot, but the slot is not stable (in migration or
  1028	 * importing state, likely because a resharding is in progress).
  1029	 *
  1030	 * CLUSTER_REDIR_DOWN_UNBOUND if the request addresses a slot which is
  1031	 * not bound to any node. In this case the cluster global state should be
  1032	 * already "down" but it is fragile to rely on the update of the global state,
  1033	 * so we also handle it here.
  1034	 *
  1035	 * CLUSTER_REDIR_DOWN_STATE and CLUSTER_REDIR_DOWN_RO_STATE if the cluster is
  1036	 * down but the user attempts to execute a command that addresses one or more keys. */
  1037	clusterNode *getNodeByQuery(client *c, int *error_code) {

  1050	    if (server.cluster_module_flags & CLUSTER_MODULE_FLAG_NO_REDIRECTION) return myself;

  1238	            if (error_code) *error_code = CLUSTER_REDIR_DOWN_RO_STATE;

  1244	        }

  1258	        if (existing_keys) {

  1263	            return getMigratingSlotDest(c->slot);

  1280	    /* Handle the read-only client case reading from a replica: if this
  1281	     * node is a replica and the request is about a hash slot our primary
  1282	     * is serving, we can reply without redirection. */
  1283	    int is_write_command =
  1284	        (cmd_flags & CMD_WRITE) || (c->cmd->proc == execCommand && (c->mstate->cmd_flags & CMD_WRITE));
  1285	    if ((c->flag.readonly || pubsubshard_included) && !is_write_command && clusterNodeIsReplica(myself) &&
  1286	        clusterNodeGetPrimary(myself) == n) {
  1287	        return myself;
  1288	    }
  1289	
  1290	    /* Base case: just return the right node. However, if this node is not
  1291	     * myself, set error_code to MOVED since we need to issue a redirection. */
  1292	    if (n != myself && error_code) *error_code = CLUSTER_REDIR_MOVED;
  1293	    return n;
  1294	}
  1295	
  1296	/* Send the client the right redirection code, according to error_code
  1297	 * that should be set to one of CLUSTER_REDIR_* macros.
  1298	 *
  1299	 * If CLUSTER_REDIR_ASK or CLUSTER_REDIR_MOVED error codes
  1300	 * are used, then the node 'n' should not be NULL, but should be the
  1301	 * node we want to mention in the redirection. Moreover hashslot should
  1302	 * be set to the hash slot that caused the redirection. */
  1303	void clusterRedirectClient(client *c, clusterNode *n, int hashslot, int error_code) {
  1304	    if (error_code == CLUSTER_REDIR_CROSS_SLOT) {
  1305	        addReplyError(c, "-CROSSSLOT Keys in request don't hash to the same slot");
  1306	    } else if (error_code == CLUSTER_REDIR_UNSTABLE) {
  1307	        /* The request spawns multiple keys in the same slot,
  1308	         * but the slot is not "stable" currently as there is
  1309	         * a migration or import in progress. */
  1310	        addReplyError(c, "-TRYAGAIN Multiple keys request during rehashing of slot");

  2729	                }

  2731	                /* Handle the case where we are importing this slot and the ownership changes */
  2732	                if (server.cluster->importing_slots_from[j] != NULL &&
  2733	                    server.cluster->importing_slots_from[j] != sender) {
  2734	                    /* Update importing_slots_from to point to the sender, if it is in the
  2735	                     * same shard as the previous slot owner */
  2736	                    if (areInSameShard(sender, server.cluster->importing_slots_from[j])) {
  2737	                        serverLog(LL_NOTICE,
  2738	                                  "Failover occurred in migration source. Update importing "
  2739	                                  "source for slot %d to node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s.",
  2740	                                  j, sender->name, sender->human_nodename, sender->shard_id);
  2741	                        server.cluster->importing_slots_from[j] = sender;
  2742	                    } else {
  2743	                        /* If the sender is from a different shard, it must be a result
  2744	                         * of deliberate operator actions. We should clear the importing
  2745	                         * state to conform to the operator's will. */
  2746	                        serverLog(LL_NOTICE, "Slot %d is no longer being imported from node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s.",
  2747	                                  j, server.cluster->importing_slots_from[j]->name,
  2748	                                  server.cluster->importing_slots_from[j]->human_nodename,
  2749	                                  server.cluster->importing_slots_from[j]->shard_id);
  2750	                        server.cluster->importing_slots_from[j] = NULL;
  2751	                    }
  2752	                }
  2753	
  2754	                clusterDelSlot(j);
  2755	                clusterAddSlot(sender, j);
  2756	                bitmapClearBit(server.cluster->owner_not_claiming_slot, j);
  2757	                clusterDoBeforeSleep(CLUSTER_TODO_SAVE_CONFIG | CLUSTER_TODO_UPDATE_STATE | CLUSTER_TODO_FSYNC_CONFIG);
  2758	            }
  2759	        } else {
  2760	            if (server.cluster->slots[j] == sender) {
  2761	                /* The slot is currently bound to the sender but the sender is no longer
  2762	                 * claiming it. We don't want to unbind the slot yet as it can cause the cluster
  2763	                 * to move to FAIL state and also throw client error. Keeping the slot bound to
  2764	                 * the previous owner will cause a few client side redirects, but won't throw
  2765	                 * any errors. We will keep track of the uncertainty in ownership to avoid
  2766	                 * propagating misinformation about this slot's ownership using UPDATE
  2767	                 * messages. */
  2768	                bitmapSetBit(server.cluster->owner_not_claiming_slot, j);
  2769	            }
  2770	
  2771	            /* If the sender doesn't claim the slot, check if we are migrating
  2772	             * any slot to its shard and if there is a primaryship change in
  2773	             * the shard. Update the migrating_slots_to state to point to the
  2774	             * sender if it has just taken over the primary role. */
  2775	            if (server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j] != NULL && server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j] != sender &&
  2776	                (server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j]->configEpoch < senderConfigEpoch ||
  2777	                 nodeIsReplica(server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j])) &&
  2778	                areInSameShard(server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j], sender)) {
  2779	                serverLog(LL_NOTICE,
  2780	                          "Failover occurred in migration target."
  2781	                          " Slot %d is now being migrated to node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s.",
  2782	                          j, sender->name, sender->human_nodename, sender->shard_id);
  2783	                server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j] = sender;
  2784	                clusterDoBeforeSleep(CLUSTER_TODO_SAVE_CONFIG | CLUSTER_TODO_UPDATE_STATE | CLUSTER_TODO_FSYNC_CONFIG);
  2785	            }
  2786	
  2787	            /* If the sender is no longer the owner of the slot, and I am a primary
  2788	             * and I am still in the process of importing the slot from the sender,
  2789	             * there are two possibilities:
  2790	             *
  2791	             * 1. I could be a replica of the target primary and missed the slot
  2792	             *    finalization step on my primary due to my primary crashing during
  2793	             *    the slot migration process.
  2794	             * 2. I could be the original primary and missed the slot finalization
  2795	             *    step entirely.
  2796	             *
  2797	             * To ensure complete slot coverage in either case, the following steps
  2798	             * will be taken:
  2799	             *
  2800	             * 1. Remove the importing state for the specific slot.
  2801	             * 2. Finalize the slot's ownership, if I am not already the owner of
  2802	             *    the slot. */
  2803	            if (nodeIsPrimary(myself) && server.cluster->importing_slots_from[j] == sender) {
  2804	                serverLog(LL_NOTICE,
  2805	                          "Slot %d is no longer being imported from node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s;"
  2806	                          " Clear my importing source for the slot.",
  2807	                          j, sender->name, sender->human_nodename, sender->shard_id);
  2808	                server.cluster->importing_slots_from[j] = NULL;
  2809	                /* Take over the slot ownership if I am not the owner yet*/
  2810	                if (server.cluster->slots[j] != myself) {
  2811	                    /* A primary reason why we are here is likely due to my primary crashing during the
  2812	                     * slot finalization process, leading me to become the new primary without
  2813	                     * inheriting the slot ownership, while the source shard continued and relinquished
  2814	                     * theslot to its old primary. Under such circumstances, the node would undergo
  2815	                     * an election and have its config epoch increased with consensus. That said, we
  2816	                     * will still explicitly bump the config epoch here to be consistent with the
  2817	                     * existing practice.
  2818	                     * Nevertheless, there are scenarios where the source shard may have transferred slot
  2819	                     * to a different shard. In these cases, the bumping of the config epoch
  2820	                     * could result in that slot assignment getting reverted. However, we consider
  2821	                     * this as a very rare case and err on the side of being consistent with the current
  2822	                     * practice. */
  2823	                    clusterDelSlot(j);
  2824	                    clusterAddSlot(myself, j);
  2825	                    clusterBumpConfigEpochWithoutConsensus();
  2826	                    clusterDoBeforeSleep(CLUSTER_TODO_SAVE_CONFIG | CLUSTER_TODO_UPDATE_STATE |
  2827	                                         CLUSTER_TODO_FSYNC_CONFIG);
  2828	                }
  2829	            }
  2830	        }
  2831	    }
  2832	
  2833	    /* After updating the slots configuration, don't do any actual change
  2834	     * in the state of the server if a module disabled Cluster
  2835	     * keys redirections. */
  2836	    if (server.cluster_module_flags & CLUSTER_MODULE_FLAG_NO_REDIRECTION) return;
  2837	
  2838	    /* Handle a special case where new_primary is not set but both sender
  2839	     * and myself own no slots and in the same shard. Set the sender as
  2840	     * the new primary if my current config epoch is lower than the
  2841	     * sender's. */
  2842	    if (!new_primary && myself->replicaof != sender && sender_slots == 0 && myself->numslots == 0 &&
  2843	        nodeEpoch(myself) < senderConfigEpoch && are_in_same_shard) {
  2844	        new_primary = sender;
  2845	    }
  2846	
  2847	    /* If the shard to which this node (myself) belongs loses all of
  2848	     * its slots, this node should become a replica of the sender if
  2849	     * one of the following conditions is true:
  2850	     *
  2851	     * 1. cluster-allow-replication-migration is enabled
  2852	     * 2. all the lost slots go to the sender and the sender belongs
  2853	     *    to this node's shard
  2854	     *
  2855	     * Note that case 2 can happen in one of the following scenarios:
  2856	     * 1) we were a primary and the sender was a replica in the same
  2857	     *    shard but just became the primary after a failover
  2858	     * 2) we were a replica and our primary lost all of its slots to
  2859	     *    the sender who was another replica in the same shard and has
  2860	     *    just become the primary after a failover
  2861	     *
  2862	     * It is also possible that the sender is a primary in a different
  2863	     * shard and our primary just had its last slot migrated to the
  2864	     * sender. In this case we don't reconfigure ourselves as a replica
  2865	     * of the sender. */
  2866	    if (new_primary && cur_primary->numslots == 0) {
  2867	        if (server.cluster_allow_replica_migration || are_in_same_shard) {
  2868	            serverLog(LL_NOTICE,
  2869	                      "Configuration change detected. Reconfiguring myself "
  2870	                      "as a replica of node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s",
  2871	                      sender->name, sender->human_nodename, sender->shard_id);
  2872	            /* Don't clear the migrating/importing states if this is a replica that
  2873	             * just gets promoted to the new primary in the shard.
  2874	             *
  2875	             * If the sender and myself are in the same shard, try psync. */
  2876	            clusterSetPrimary(sender, !are_in_same_shard, !are_in_same_shard);
  2877	            clusterDoBeforeSleep(CLUSTER_TODO_SAVE_CONFIG | CLUSTER_TODO_UPDATE_STATE | CLUSTER_TODO_FSYNC_CONFIG |
  2878	                                 CLUSTER_TODO_BROADCAST_ALL);
  2879	        } else if (nodeIsPrimary(myself) && (sender_slots >= migrated_our_slots) && !are_in_same_shard) {
  2880	            /* When all our slots are lost to the sender and the sender belongs to
  2881	             * a different shard, this is likely due to a client triggered slot
  2882	             * migration. Don't reconfigure this node to migrate to the new shard
  2883	             * in this case. */
  2884	            serverLog(LL_NOTICE,
  2885	                      "My last slot was migrated to node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s. I am now an empty primary.",
  2886	                      sender->name, sender->human_nodename, sender->shard_id);
  2887	            /* We may still have dirty slots when we became a empty primary due to
  2888	             * a bad migration.
  2889	             *
  2890	             * In order to maintain a consistent state between keys and slots
  2891	             * we need to remove all the keys from the slots we lost. */
  2892	            delete_dirty_slots = 1;
  2893	        }
  2894	    } else if (dirty_slots_count) {
  2895	        /* If we are here, we received an update message which removed
  2896	         * ownership for certain slots we still have keys about, but still
  2897	         * we are serving some slots, so this primary node was not demoted to
  2898	         * a replica.
  2899	         *
  2900	         * In order to maintain a consistent state between keys and slots
  2901	         * we need to remove all the keys from the slots we lost. */
  2902	        delete_dirty_slots = 1;
  2903	    }
  2904	
  2905	    if (delete_dirty_slots) {

  6039	static inline void removeAllNotOwnedShardChannelSubscriptions(void) {

  6050	 * REPLICA nodes handling

  6053	/* Set the specified node 'n' as primary for this node.
  6054	 * If this node is currently a primary, it is turned into a replica. */
  6055	static void clusterSetPrimary(clusterNode *n, int closeSlots, int full_sync_required) {
  6056	    serverAssert(n != myself);
  6057	    serverAssert(myself->numslots == 0);
  6058	
  6059	    if (clusterNodeIsPrimary(myself)) {
  6060	        myself->flags &= ~(CLUSTER_NODE_PRIMARY | CLUSTER_NODE_MIGRATE_TO);
  6061	        myself->flags |= CLUSTER_NODE_REPLICA;
  6062	    } else {
  6063	        if (myself->replicaof) clusterNodeRemoveReplica(myself->replicaof, myself);
  6064	    }
  6065	    if (closeSlots) clusterCloseAllSlots();
  6066	    myself->replicaof = n;
  6067	    updateShardId(myself, n->shard_id);
  6068	    clusterNodeAddReplica(n, myself);
  6069	    replicationSetPrimary(n->ip, getNodeDefaultReplicationPort(n), full_sync_required);
  6070	    removeAllNotOwnedShardChannelSubscriptions();
  6071	    resetManualFailover();
  6072	
  6073	    if (server.cluster->failover_auth_time) {
  6074	        /* Since we have changed to a new primary node, the previously set
  6075	         * failover_auth_time should no longer be used, whether it is in
  6076	         * progress or timed out. */
  6077	        server.cluster->failover_auth_time = 0;
  6078	    }
  6079	}

  2618	/* Reconfigure the specified node 'n' as a primary. This function is called when
  2619	 * a node that we believed to be a replica is now acting as primary in order to
  2620	 * update the state of the node. */
  2621	void clusterSetNodeAsPrimary(clusterNode *n) {
  2622	    if (clusterNodeIsPrimary(n)) return;
  2623	
  2624	    if (n->replicaof) {
  2625	        clusterNodeRemoveReplica(n->replicaof, n);
  2626	        if (n != myself) n->flags |= CLUSTER_NODE_MIGRATE_TO;
  2627	    }
  2628	    n->flags &= ~CLUSTER_NODE_REPLICA;
  2629	    n->flags |= CLUSTER_NODE_PRIMARY;
  2630	    n->replicaof = NULL;
  2631	
  2632	    /* Update config and state. */
  2633	    clusterDoBeforeSleep(CLUSTER_TODO_SAVE_CONFIG | CLUSTER_TODO_UPDATE_STATE);
  2634	}

  2636	/* This function is called when we receive a primary configuration via a
  2637	 * PING, PONG or UPDATE packet. What we receive is a node, a configEpoch of the
  2638	 * node, and the set of slots claimed under this configEpoch.

  1328	/* This function is called by the function processing clients incrementally
  1329	 * to detect timeouts, in order to handle the following case:
  1330	 *
  1331	 * 1) A client blocks with BLPOP or similar blocking operation.
  1332	 * 2) The primary migrates the hash slot elsewhere or turns into a replica.
  1333	 * 3) The client may remain blocked forever (or up to the max timeout time)
  1334	 *    waiting for a key change that will never happen.
  1335	 *
  1336	 * If the client is found to be blocked into a hash slot this node no
  1337	 * longer handles, the client is sent a redirection error, and the function
  1338	 * returns 1. Otherwise 0 is returned and no operation is performed. */
  1339	int clusterRedirectBlockedClientIfNeeded(client *c) {
  1340	    clusterNode *myself = getMyClusterNode();
  1341	    if (c->flag.blocked && (c->bstate->btype == BLOCKED_LIST || c->bstate->btype == BLOCKED_ZSET ||
  1342	                            c->bstate->btype == BLOCKED_STREAM || c->bstate->btype == BLOCKED_MODULE)) {
  1343	        dictEntry *de;
  1344	        dictIterator *di;
  1345	
  1346	        /* If the client is blocked on module, but not on a specific key,
  1347	         * don't unblock it. */
  1348	        if (c->bstate->btype == BLOCKED_MODULE && !moduleClientIsBlockedOnKeys(c)) return 0;
  1349	
  1350	        /* If the cluster is down, unblock the client with the right error.
  1351	         * If the cluster is configured to allow reads on cluster down, we
  1352	         * still want to emit this error since a write will be required
  1353	         * to unblock them which may never come.  */
  1354	        if (!isClusterHealthy()) {
  1355	            clusterRedirectClient(c, NULL, 0, CLUSTER_REDIR_DOWN_STATE);
  1356	            return 1;
  1357	        }
  1358	
  1359	        /* All keys must belong to the same slot, so check first key only. */
  1360	        di = dictGetIterator(c->bstate->keys);
  1361	        if ((de = dictNext(di)) != NULL) {
  1362	            robj *key = dictGetKey(de);
  1363	            int slot = keyHashSlot((char *)key->ptr, sdslen(key->ptr));
  1364	            serverAssert(slot == c->slot);
  1365	            clusterNode *node = getNodeBySlot(slot);
  1366	
  1367	            /* if the client is read-only and attempting to access key that our
  1368	             * replica can handle, allow it. */
  1369	            if (c->flag.readonly && !(c->lastcmd->flags & CMD_WRITE) && clusterNodeIsReplica(myself) &&
  1370	                clusterNodeGetPrimary(myself) == node) {
  1371	                node = myself;
  1372	            }
  1373	
  1374	            /* We send an error and unblock the client if:
  1375	             * 1) The slot is unassigned, emitting a cluster down error.
  1376	             * 2) The slot is neither handled by this node, nor being imported. */
  1377	            if (node != myself && getImportingSlotSource(slot) == NULL) {
  1378	                if (node == NULL) {
  1379	                    clusterRedirectClient(c, NULL, 0, CLUSTER_REDIR_DOWN_UNBOUND);
  1380	                } else {
  1381	                    clusterRedirectClient(c, node, slot, CLUSTER_REDIR_MOVED);
  1382	                }
  1383	                dictReleaseIterator(di);
  1384	                return 1;
  1385	            }
  1386	        }
  1387	        dictReleaseIterator(di);
  1388	    }
  1389	    return 0;
  1390	}

  7615	/* Encode open slot states into an sds string to be persisted as an aux field in RDB. */
  7616	sds clusterEncodeOpenSlotsAuxField(int rdbflags) {
  7617	    if (!server.cluster_enabled) return NULL;
  7618	
  7619	    /* Open slots should not be persisted to an RDB file. This data is intended only for full sync. */
  7620	    if ((rdbflags & RDBFLAGS_REPLICATION) == 0) return NULL;
  7621	
  7622	    sds s = NULL;
  7623	
  7624	    for (int i = 0; i < 2; i++) {
  7625	        clusterNode **nodes_ptr;
  7626	        if (i == 0) {
  7627	            nodes_ptr = server.cluster->importing_slots_from;
  7628	        } else {
  7629	            nodes_ptr = server.cluster->migrating_slots_to;
  7630	        }
  7631	
  7632	        for (int j = 0; j < CLUSTER_SLOTS; j++) {
  7633	            if (nodes_ptr[j] == NULL) continue;
  7634	            if (s == NULL) s = sdsempty();
  7635	            s = sdscatfmt(s, "%i%s", j, (i == 0) ? "<" : ">");
  7636	            s = sdscatlen(s, nodes_ptr[j]->name, CLUSTER_NAMELEN);
  7637	            s = sdscatlen(s, ",", 1);
  7638	        }
  7639	    }
  7640	
  7641	    return s;
  7642	}

  7644	/* Decode the open slot aux field and restore the in-memory slot states. */
  7645	int clusterDecodeOpenSlotsAuxField(int rdbflags, sds s) {
  7646	    if (!server.cluster_enabled || s == NULL) return C_OK;
  7647	
  7648	    /* Open slots should not be loaded from a persisted RDB file, but only from a full sync. */
  7649	    if ((rdbflags & RDBFLAGS_REPLICATION) == 0) return C_OK;
  7650	
  7651	    while (*s) {
  7652	        /* Extract slot number */
  7653	        int slot = atoi(s);
  7654	        if (slot < 0 || slot >= CLUSTER_SLOTS) return C_ERR;
  7655	
  7656	        while (*s && *s != '<' && *s != '>') s++;
  7657	        if (*s != '<' && *s != '>') return C_ERR;
  7658	
  7659	        /* Determine if it's an importing or migrating slot */
  7660	        int is_importing = (*s == '<');
  7661	        s++;
  7662	
  7663	        /* Extract the node name */
  7664	        char node_name[CLUSTER_NAMELEN];
  7665	        int k = 0;
  7666	        while (*s && *s != ',' && k < CLUSTER_NAMELEN) {
  7667	            node_name[k++] = *s++;
  7668	        }
  7669	
  7670	        /* Ensure the node name is of the correct length */
  7671	        if (k != CLUSTER_NAMELEN || *s != ',') return C_ERR;
  7672	
  7673	        /* Move to the next slot */
  7674	        s++;
  7675	
  7676	        /* Find the corresponding node */
  7677	        clusterNode *node = clusterLookupNode(node_name, CLUSTER_NAMELEN);
  7678	        if (!node) {
  7679	            /* Create a new node if not found */
  7680	            node = createClusterNode(node_name, 0);
  7681	            clusterAddNode(node);
  7682	        }
  7683	
  7684	        /* Set the slot state */
  7685	        if (is_importing) {
  7686	            server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot] = node;
  7687	        } else {
  7688	            server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot] = node;
  7689	        }
  7690	    }
  7691	    return C_OK;
  7692	}

  6845	/* clusterParseSetSlotCommand validates the arguments of the CLUSTER SETSLOT command,
  6846	 * extracts the target slot number (slot_out), and determines the target node (node_out)
  6847	 * if applicable. It also calculates a timeout value (timeout_out) based on an optional
  6848	 * timeout argument. If provided, the timeout is added to the current time to obtain an
  6849	 * absolute timestamp; if omitted, the default timeout CLUSTER_OPERATION_TIMEOUT is used;
  6850	 * if set to 0, it indicates no timeout. The function returns 1 if successful, and 0
  6851	 * otherwise, after sending an error message to the client. */
  6852	int clusterParseSetSlotCommand(client *c, int *slot_out, clusterNode **node_out, mstime_t *timeout_out) {
  6853	    int slot = -1;
  6854	    clusterNode *n = NULL;
  6855	    mstime_t timeout = commandTimeSnapshot() + CLUSTER_OPERATION_TIMEOUT;
  6856	    int optarg_pos = 0;

  6858	    /* Allow primaries to replicate "CLUSTER SETSLOT" */
  6859	    if (!c->flag.primary && nodeIsReplica(myself)) {
  6860	        addReplyError(c, "Please use SETSLOT only with masters.");
  6861	        return 0;
  6862	    }
  6863	
  6864	    /* If 'myself' is a replica, 'c' must be the primary client. */
  6865	    serverAssert(!nodeIsReplica(myself) || c == server.primary);
  6866

  6871	        if (nodeIsPrimary(myself) && server.cluster->slots[slot] != myself) {

  6878	            return 0;

  6881	            addReplyError(c, "Target node is not a master");
  6882	            return 0;
  6883	        }

  6916	         * make sure there are no longer local keys for this hash slot. */
  6917	        if (server.cluster->slots[slot] == myself && n != myself) {

  6920	                                    "Can't assign hashslot %d to a different node "

  6949	void clusterCommandSetSlot(client *c) {
  6950	    int slot;
  6951	    mstime_t timeout_ms;
  6952	    clusterNode *n;
  6953	
  6954	    if (!clusterParseSetSlotCommand(c, &slot, &n, &timeout_ms)) return;
  6955	
  6956	    /* Enhance cluster topology change resilience against primary failures by
  6957	     * replicating SETSLOT before execution.
  6958	     *
  6959	     * Cluster topology changes such slot ownership and migrating states must
  6960	     * be replicated to replicas before applying them to the primary. This
  6961	     * guarantees that after a command is successfully executed, the new state
  6962	     * won't be lost due to a primary node failure. The following example
  6963	     * illustrates how a cluster state can be lost during slot ownership
  6964	     * finalization:
  6965	     *
  6966	     * When finalizing the slot, the target primary node B might send a cluster
  6967	     * PONG to the source primary node A before the SETSLOT command is replicated
  6968	     * to replica node B'. If primary node B crashes at this point, B' will be in
  6969	     * the importing state and the slot will have no owner.
  6970	     *
  6971	     * To mitigate this issue, the following order needs to be enforced for slot
  6972	     * migration finalization such that the replicas finalize the slot ownership
  6973	     * before the primary:
  6974	     *
  6975	     * 1. Client C issues SETSLOT n NODE B against node B.
  6976	     * 2. Primary B replicates `SETSLOT n NODE B` to all of its replicas (e.g., B', B'').
  6977	     * 3. Upon replication completion, primary B executes `SETSLOT n NODE B` and
  6978	     *    returns success to client C.
  6979	     * 4. The following steps can happen in parallel:
  6980	     *   a. Client C issues `SETSLOT n NODE B` against primary A.
  6981	     *   b. Primary B gossips its new slot ownership to the cluster (including A, A', etc.).
  6982	     *
  6983	     * This ensures that all replicas have the latest topology information, enabling
  6984	     * a reliable slot ownership transfer even if the primary node went down during
  6985	     * the process. */
  6986	    if (nodeIsPrimary(myself) && myself->num_replicas != 0 && !c->flag.replication_done) {
  6987	        /* Iterate through the list of replicas to check if there are any running
  6988	         * version 7.2 or older. Replicas running on these versions do
  6989	         * not support the CLUSTER SETSLOT command on replicas. If such a replica
  6990	         * is found, we should skip the replication and fall back to the old
  6991	         * non-replicated behavior.*/
  6992	        listIter li;
  6993	        listNode *ln;
  6994	        int num_eligible_replicas = 0;
  6995	        listRewind(server.replicas, &li);
  6996	        while ((ln = listNext(&li))) {
  6997	            client *r = ln->value;
  6998	
  6999	            /* We think that when the command comes in, the primary only needs to
  7000	             * wait for the online replicas. The admin can easily check if there
  7001	             * are replicas that are down for an extended period of time. If they
  7002	             * decide to move forward anyways, we should not block it. If a replica
  7003	             * failed right before the replication and was not included in the
  7004	             * replication, it would also unlikely win the election.
  7005	             *
  7006	             * And 0x702ff is 7.2.255, we only support new versions in this case. */
  7007	            if (r->repl_data->repl_state == REPLICA_STATE_ONLINE && r->repl_data->replica_version > 0x702ff) {
  7008	                num_eligible_replicas++;
  7009	            }
  7010	        }
  7011	
  7012	        if (num_eligible_replicas != 0) {
  7013	            forceCommandPropagation(c, PROPAGATE_REPL);
  7014	            /* We are a primary and this is the first time we see this `SETSLOT`
  7015	             * command. Force-replicate the command to all of our replicas
  7016	             * first and only on success will we handle the command.
  7017	             * Note that
  7018	             * 1. All replicas are expected to ack the replication within the given timeout
  7019	             * 2. The repl offset target is set to the primary's current repl offset + 1.
  7020	             *    There is no concern of partial replication because replicas always
  7021	             *    ack the repl offset at the command boundary. */
  7022	            blockClientForReplicaAck(c, timeout_ms, server.primary_repl_offset + 1, num_eligible_replicas, 0);
  7023	            /* Mark client as pending command for execution after replication to replicas. */
  7024	            c->flag.pending_command = 1;
  7025	            replicationRequestAckFromReplicas();
  7026	            return;
  7027	        }
  7028	    }
  7029	
  7030	    /* Slot states have been updated on the compatible replicas (if any).
  7031	     * Now execute the command on the primary. */
  7032	    if (!strcasecmp(c->argv[3]->ptr, "migrating")) {
  7033	        serverLog(LL_NOTICE, "Migrating slot %d to node %.40s (%s)", slot, n->name, n->human_nodename);
  7034	        server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot] = n;
  7035	    } else if (!strcasecmp(c->argv[3]->ptr, "importing")) {

   641	/* block a client for replica acknowledgement */
   642	void blockClientForReplicaAck(client *c, mstime_t timeout, long long offset, long numreplicas, int numlocal) {
   643	    initClientBlockingState(c);
   644	    c->bstate->timeout = timeout;
   645	    c->bstate->reploffset = offset;
   646	    c->bstate->numreplicas = numreplicas;
   647	    c->bstate->numlocal = numlocal;
   648	    listAddNodeHead(server.clients_waiting_acks, c);
   649	    /* Note that we remember the linked list node where the client is stored,
   650	     * this way removing the client in unblockClientWaitingReplicas() will not
   651	     * require a linear scan, but just a constant time operation. */
   652	    serverAssert(c->bstate->client_waiting_acks_list_node == NULL);
   653	    c->bstate->client_waiting_acks_list_node = listFirst(server.clients_waiting_acks);
   654	    blockClient(c, BLOCKED_WAIT);
   655	}
   656	
   657	/* Postpone client from executing a command. For example the server might be busy
   658	 * requesting to avoid processing clients commands which will be processed later
   659	 * when the it is ready to accept them. */
   660	void blockPostponeClient(client *c) {
   661	    initClientBlockingState(c);
   662	    c->bstate->timeout = 0;
   663	    blockClient(c, BLOCKED_POSTPONE);
   664	    listAddNodeTail(server.postponed_clients, c);
   665	    serverAssert(c->bstate->postponed_list_node == NULL);
   666	    c->bstate->postponed_list_node = listLast(server.postponed_clients);
   667	    /* Mark this client to execute its command */
   668	    c->flag.pending_command = 1;
   669	}
   670	
   671	/* Block client due to shutdown command */
   672	void blockClientShutdown(client *c) {
   673	    initClientBlockingState(c);
   674	    c->bstate->timeout = 0;
   675	    blockClient(c, BLOCKED_SHUTDOWN);
   676	}
   677	
   678	/* Unblock a client once a specific key became available for it.
   679	 * This function will remove the client from the list of clients blocked on this key
   680	 * and also remove the key from the dictionary of keys this client is blocked on.
   681	 * in case the client has a command pending it will process it immediately.  */
   682	static void unblockClientOnKey(client *c, robj *key) {
   683	    dictEntry *de;
   684	
   685	    de = dictFind(c->bstate->keys, key);
   686	    releaseBlockedEntry(c, de, 1);
   687	
   688	    /* Only in case of blocking API calls, we might be blocked on several keys.
   689	       however we should force unblock the entire blocking keys */
   690	    serverAssert(c->bstate->btype == BLOCKED_STREAM || c->bstate->btype == BLOCKED_LIST ||
   691	                 c->bstate->btype == BLOCKED_ZSET);
   692	
   693	    /* We need to unblock the client before calling processCommandAndResetClient
   694	     * because it checks the CLIENT_BLOCKED flag */
   695	    unblockClient(c, 0);
   696	    /* In case this client was blocked on keys during command
   697	     * we need to re process the command again */
   698	    if (c->flag.pending_command) {
   699	        c->flag.pending_command = 0;
   700	        c->flag.reexecuting_command = 1;
   701	        /* We want the command processing and the unblock handler (see RM_Call 'K' option)
   702	         * to run atomically, this is why we must enter the execution unit here before
   703	         * running the command, and exit the execution unit after calling the unblock handler (if exists).
   704	         * Notice that we also must set the current client so it will be available
   705	         * when we will try to send the client side caching notification (done on 'afterCommand'). */
   706	        client *old_client = server.current_client;
   707	        server.current_client = c;
   708	        enterExecutionUnit(1, 0);
   709	        processCommandAndResetClient(c);
   710	        if (!c->flag.blocked) {
   711	            if (c->flag.module) {
   712	                moduleCallCommandUnblockedHandler(c);
   713	            } else {
   714	                queueClientForReprocessing(c);
   715	            }
   716	        }
   717	        exitExecutionUnit();
   718	        afterCommand(c);
   719	        /* Clear the reexecuting_command flag after the proc is executed. */
   720	        c->flag.reexecuting_command = 0;
   721	        server.current_client = old_client;
   722	    }
   723	}
   724	
   725	/* Unblock a client blocked on the specific key from module context.
   726	 * This function will try to serve the module call, and in case it succeeds,
   727	 * it will add the client to the list of module unblocked clients which will
   728	 * be processed in moduleHandleBlockedClients. */
   729	static void moduleUnblockClientOnKey(client *c, robj *key) {
   730	    long long prev_error_replies = server.stat_total_error_replies;
   731	    client *old_client = server.current_client;
   732	    server.current_client = c;
   733	    monotime replyTimer;
   734	    elapsedStart(&replyTimer);
   735	
   736	    if (moduleTryServeClientBlockedOnKey(c, key)) {
   737	        updateStatsOnUnblock(c, 0, elapsedUs(replyTimer),
   738	                             ((server.stat_total_error_replies != prev_error_replies) ? ERROR_COMMAND_FAILED : 0));
   739	        moduleUnblockClient(c);
   740	    }
   741	    /* We need to call afterCommand even if the client was not unblocked
   742	     * in order to propagate any changes that could have been done inside
   743	     * moduleTryServeClientBlockedOnKey */
   744	    afterCommand(c);
   745	    server.current_client = old_client;
   746	}
   747	
   748	/* Unblock a client which is currently Blocked on and provided a timeout.
   749	 * The implementation will first reply to the blocked client with null response
   750	 * or, in case of module blocked client the timeout callback will be used.
   751	 * In this case since we might have a command pending
   752	 * we want to remove the pending flag to indicate we already responded to the
   753	 * command with timeout reply. */
   754	void unblockClientOnTimeout(client *c) {
   755	    /* The client has been unlocked (in the moduleUnblocked list), return ASAP. */
   756	    if (c->bstate->btype == BLOCKED_MODULE && isModuleClientUnblocked(c)) return;
   757	
   758	    replyToBlockedClientTimedOut(c);
   759	    if (c->flag.pending_command) c->flag.pending_command = 0;
   760	    unblockClient(c, 1);
   761	}
   762	
   763	/* Unblock a client which is currently Blocked with error.
   764	 * If err_str is provided it will be used to reply to the blocked client */
   765	void unblockClientOnError(client *c, const char *err_str) {
   766	    if (err_str) addReplyError(c, err_str);
   767	    updateStatsOnUnblock(c, 0, 0, ERROR_COMMAND_REJECTED);
   768	    if (c->flag.pending_command) c->flag.pending_command = 0;
   769	    unblockClient(c, 1);
   770	}
   771	
   772	void blockedBeforeSleep(void) {
   773	    /* Handle precise timeouts of blocked clients. */
   774	    handleBlockedClientsTimeout();
   775

   132	    if (raxSize(server.clients_timeout_table) == 0) return;
   133	    uint64_t now = mstime();
   134	    raxIterator ri;
   135	    raxStart(&ri, server.clients_timeout_table);
   136	    raxSeek(&ri, "^", NULL, 0);

   145	        raxRemove(server.clients_timeout_table, ri.key, ri.key_len, NULL);
   146	        raxSeek(&ri, "^", NULL, 0);
   147	    }
   148	    raxStop(&ri);
   149	}

  3463	/* Commands arriving from the primary client or AOF client, should never be rejected. */
  3464	int mustObeyClient(client *c) {
  3465	    return c->id == CLIENT_ID_AOF || c->flag.primary;
  3466	}
  3467	
  3468	static int shouldPropagate(int target) {
  3469	    if (!server.replication_allowed || target == PROPAGATE_NONE || server.loading) return 0;
  3470	
  3471	    if (target & PROPAGATE_AOF) {
  3472	        if (server.aof_state != AOF_OFF) return 1;
  3473	    }
  3474	    if (target & PROPAGATE_REPL) {
  3475	        if (server.primary_host == NULL && (server.repl_backlog || listLength(server.replicas) != 0)) return 1;
  3476	    }
  3477	
  3478	    return 0;
  3479	}
  3480	
  3481	/* Propagate the specified command (in the context of the specified database id)
  3482	 * to AOF and replicas.
  3483	 *
  3484	 * flags are an xor between:
  3485	 * + PROPAGATE_NONE (no propagation of command at all)
  3486	 * + PROPAGATE_AOF (propagate into the AOF file if is enabled)
  3487	 * + PROPAGATE_REPL (propagate into the replication link)
  3488	 *
  3489	 * This is an internal low-level function and should not be called!
  3490	 *
  3491	 * The API for propagating commands is alsoPropagate().
  3492	 *
  3493	 * dbid value of -1 is saved to indicate that the called do not want
  3494	 * to replicate SELECT for this command (used for database neutral commands).
  3495	 */
  3496	static void propagateNow(int dbid, robj **argv, int argc, int target) {
  3497	    if (!shouldPropagate(target)) return;
  3498	
  3499	    /* This needs to be unreachable since the dataset should be fixed during
  3500	     * replica pause (otherwise data may be lost during a failover).
  3501	     *
  3502	     * Though, there are exceptions:
  3503	     *
  3504	     * 1. We allow write commands that were queued up before and after to
  3505	     *    execute, if a CLIENT PAUSE executed during a transaction, we will
  3506	     *    track the state, the CLIENT PAUSE takes effect only after a transaction
  3507	     *    has finished.
  3508	     * 2. Primary loses a slot during the pause, deletes all keys and replicates
  3509	     *    DEL to its replicas. In this case, we will track the state, the dirty
  3510	     *    slots will be deleted in the end without affecting the data consistency.
  3511	     *
  3512	     * Note that case 2 can happen in one of the following scenarios:
  3513	     * 1) The primary waits for the replica to replicate before exiting, see
  3514	     *    shutdown-timeout in conf for more details. In this case, primary lost
  3515	     *    a slot during the SIGTERM waiting.
  3516	     * 2) The primary waits for the replica to replicate during a manual failover.
  3517	     *    In this case, primary lost a slot during the pausing.
  3518	     * 3) The primary was paused by CLIENT PAUSE, and lost a slot during the
  3519	     *    pausing. */
  3520	    serverAssert(!isPausedActions(PAUSE_ACTION_REPLICA) || server.client_pause_in_transaction ||
  3521	                 server.server_del_keys_in_slot);
  3522	
  3523	    if (server.aof_state != AOF_OFF && target & PROPAGATE_AOF) feedAppendOnlyFile(dbid, argv, argc);
  3524	    if (target & PROPAGATE_REPL) replicationFeedReplicas(dbid, argv, argc);
  3525	}
  3526	
  3527	/* Used inside commands to schedule the propagation of additional commands
  3528	 * after the current command is propagated to AOF / Replication.
  3529	 *
  3530	 * dbid is the database ID the command should be propagated into.
  3531	 * Arguments of the command to propagate are passed as an array of
  3532	 * Objects pointers of len 'argc', using the 'argv' vector.
  3533	 *
  3534	 * The function does not take a reference to the passed 'argv' vector,
  3535	 * so it is up to the caller to release the passed argv (but it is usually
  3536	 * stack allocated).  The function automatically increments ref count of
  3537	 * passed objects, so the caller does not need to. */
  3538	void alsoPropagate(int dbid, robj **argv, int argc, int target) {
  3539	    robj **argvcopy;
  3540	    int j;
  3541	
  3542	    if (!shouldPropagate(target)) return;
  3543	
  3544	    argvcopy = zmalloc(sizeof(robj *) * argc);
  3545	    for (j = 0; j < argc; j++) {
  3546	        argvcopy[j] = argv[j];
  3547	        incrRefCount(argv[j]);
  3548	    }
  3549	    serverOpArrayAppend(&server.also_propagate, dbid, argvcopy, argc, target);
  3550	}
  3551	
  3552	/* It is possible to call the function forceCommandPropagation() inside a
  3553	 * command implementation in order to to force the propagation of a
  3554	 * specific command execution into AOF / Replication. */
  3555	void forceCommandPropagation(client *c, int flags) {
  3556	    serverAssert(c->cmd->flags & (CMD_WRITE | CMD_MAY_REPLICATE));
  3557	    if (flags & PROPAGATE_REPL) c->flag.force_repl = 1;
  3558	    if (flags & PROPAGATE_AOF) c->flag.force_aof = 1;
  3559	}
  3560	
  3561	/* Avoid that the executed command is propagated at all. This way we
  3562	 * are free to just propagate what we want using the alsoPropagate()
  3563	 * API. */
  3564	void preventCommandPropagation(client *c) {
  3565	    c->flag.prevent_prop = 1;
  3566	}

  3559	/* This function calls processCommand(), but also performs a few sub tasks
  3560	 * for the client that are useful in that context:
  3561	 *
  3562	 * 1. It sets the current client to the client 'c'.
  3563	 * 2. calls commandProcessed() if the command was handled.
  3564	 *
  3565	 * The function returns C_ERR in case the client was freed as a side effect
  3566	 * of processing the command, otherwise C_OK is returned. */
  3567	int processCommandAndResetClient(client *c) {
  3568	    int deadclient = 0;
  3569	    client *old_client = server.current_client;
  3570	    server.current_client = c;
  3571	    if (processCommand(c) == C_OK) {
  3572	        commandProcessed(c);
  3573	        /* Update the client's memory to include output buffer growth following the

  3583	     * we will return 1 to our caller which will falsely indicate the client

  3590	    return deadclient ? C_ERR : C_OK;

  3590	/* Handle the alsoPropagate() API to handle commands that want to propagate
  3591	 * multiple separated commands. Note that alsoPropagate() is not affected
  3592	 * by CLIENT_PREVENT_PROP flag. */
  3593	static void propagatePendingCommands(void) {
  3594	    if (server.also_propagate.numops == 0) return;
  3595	
  3596	    int j;
  3597	    serverOp *rop;
  3598	
  3599	    /* If we got here it means we have finished an execution-unit.
  3600	     * If that unit has caused propagation of multiple commands, they
  3601	     * should be propagated as a transaction */
  3602	    int transaction = server.also_propagate.numops > 1;
  3603	
  3604	    /* In case a command that may modify random keys was run *directly*
  3605	     * (i.e. not from within a script, MULTI/EXEC, RM_Call, etc.) we want
  3606	     * to avoid using a transaction (much like active-expire) */
  3607	    if (server.current_client && server.current_client->cmd &&
  3608	        server.current_client->cmd->flags & CMD_TOUCHES_ARBITRARY_KEYS) {
  3609	        transaction = 0;
  3610	    }
  3611	
  3612	    if (transaction) {
  3613	        /* We use dbid=-1 to indicate we do not want to replicate SELECT.
  3614	         * It'll be inserted together with the next command (inside the MULTI) */

  3633	 * Execution unit is a code that should be done atomically.
  3634	 * Execution units can be nested and do not necessarily start with a server command.
  3635	 *
  3636	 * For example the following is a logical unit:
  3637	 *   active expire ->
  3638	 *      trigger del notification of some module ->
  3639	 *          accessing a key ->
  3640	 *              trigger key miss notification of some other module
  3641	 *
  3642	 * What we want to achieve is that the entire execution unit will be done atomically,
  3643	 * currently with respect to replication and post jobs, but in the future there might
  3644	 * be other considerations. So we basically want the `postUnitOperations` to trigger
  3645	 * after the entire chain finished. */
  3646	void postExecutionUnitOperations(void) {

  3653	    propagatePendingCommands();

/* Update local open slot state after receiving a claim for the slot owner.
 *
 * This is needed not only when the owner changes in this call, but also when
 * the slot was already bound to the sender. The latter can happen if an UPDATE
 * message or an earlier gossip packet already installed the new owner before we
 * process the packet that should refresh the migration endpoint. Without doing
 * this for an already-known owner, importing state can keep pointing at an old
 * primary after a source-shard failover. */
static int clusterUpdateOpenSlotStateOnOwnerClaim(int slot, clusterNode *sender, int are_in_same_shard) {
    int updated = 0;

    /* If the sender who claims this slot is not in the same shard,
     * it must be a result of deliberate operator actions. Therefore,
     * we should honor it and clear the outstanding migrating_slots_to
     * state for the slot. Otherwise, we are looking at a failover within
     * the same shard and we should retain the migrating_slots_to state
     * for the slot in question. */
    if (server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot] != NULL) {
        if (!are_in_same_shard) {
            serverLog(LL_NOTICE, "Slot %d is no longer being migrated to node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s.",
                      slot, server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot]->name,
                      server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot]->human_nodename,
                      server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot]->shard_id);
            server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot] = NULL;
            updated = 1;
        }
    }

    /* Handle the case where we are importing this slot and the ownership changes. */
    if (server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot] != NULL && server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot] != sender) {
        /* Update importing_slots_from to point to the sender, if it is in the
         * same shard as the previous slot owner. */
        if (areInSameShard(sender, server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot])) {
            serverLog(LL_NOTICE,
                      "Failover occurred in migration source. Update importing "
                      "source for slot %d to node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s.",
                      slot, sender->name, sender->human_nodename, sender->shard_id);
            server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot] = sender;
        } else {
            /* If the sender is from a different shard, it must be a result
             * of deliberate operator actions. We should clear the importing
             * state to conform to the operator'"'"'s will. */
            serverLog(LL_NOTICE, "Slot %d is no longer being imported from node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s.",
                      slot, server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot]->name,
                      server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot]->human_nodename,
                      server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot]->shard_id);
            server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot] = NULL;
        }
        updated = 1;
    }

    return updated;
}

     clusterDoBeforeSleep(CLUSTER_TODO_SAVE_CONFIG | CLUSTER_TODO_UPDATE_STATE);
 }
 
+
+/* Update local open slot state after receiving a claim for the slot owner.
+ *
+ * This is needed not only when the owner changes in this call, but also when
+ * the slot was already bound to the sender. The latter can happen if an UPDATE
+ * message or an earlier gossip packet already installed the new owner before we
+ * process the packet that should refresh the migration endpoint. Without doing
+ * this for an already-known owner, importing state can keep pointing at an old
+ * primary after a source-shard failover. */
+static int clusterUpdateOpenSlotStateOnOwnerClaim(int slot, clusterNode *sender, int are_in_same_shard) {
+    int updated = 0;
+
+    /* If the sender who claims this slot is not in the same shard,
+     * it must be a result of deliberate operator actions. Therefore,
+     * we should honor it and clear the outstanding migrating_slots_to
+     * state for the slot. Otherwise, we are looking at a failover within
+     * the same shard and we should retain the migrating_slots_to state
+     * for the slot in question. */
+    if (server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot] != NULL) {
+        if (!are_in_same_shard) {
+            serverLog(LL_NOTICE, "Slot %d is no longer being migrated to node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s.",
+                      slot, server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot]->name,
+                      server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot]->human_nodename,
+                      server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot]->shard_id);
+            server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot] = NULL;
+            updated = 1;
+        }
+    }
+
+    /* Handle the case where we are importing this slot and the ownership changes. */
+    if (server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot] != NULL && server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot] != sender) {
+        /* Update importing_slots_from to point to the sender, if it is in the
+         * same shard as the previous slot owner. */
+        if (areInSameShard(sender, server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot])) {
+            serverLog(LL_NOTICE,
+                      "Failover occurred in migration source. Update importing "
+                      "source for slot %d to node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s.",
+                      slot, sender->name, sender->human_nodename, sender->shard_id);
+            server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot] = sender;
+        } else {
+            /* If the sender is from a different shard, it must be a result
+             * of deliberate operator actions. We should clear the importing
+             * state to conform to the operator's will. */
+            serverLog(LL_NOTICE, "Slot %d is no longer being imported from node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s.",
+                      slot, server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot]->name,
+                      server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot]->human_nodename,
+                      server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot]->shard_id);
+            server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot] = NULL;
+        }
+        updated = 1;
+    }
+
+    return updated;
+}
+

  * PING, PONG or UPDATE packet. What we receive is a node, a configEpoch of the
  * node, and the set of slots claimed under this configEpoch.

+     * it must be a result of deliberate operator actions. Therefore,
+     * we should honor it and clear the outstanding migrating_slots_to
+     * state for the slot. Otherwise, we are looking at a failover within
+     * the same shard and we should retain the migrating_slots_to state
+     * for the slot in question. */
+    if (server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot] != NULL) {
+        if (!are_in_same_shard) {
+            serverLog(LL_NOTICE, "Slot %d is no longer being migrated to node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s.",
+                      slot, server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot]->name,
+                      server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot]->human_nodename,
+                      server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot]->shard_id);
+            server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot] = NULL;
+            updated = 1;
+        }
+    }
+
+    /* Handle the case where we are importing this slot and the ownership changes. */
+    if (server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot] != NULL && server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot] != sender) {
+        /* Update importing_slots_from to point to the sender, if it is in the
+         * same shard as the previous slot owner. */
+        if (areInSameShard(sender, server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot])) {
+            serverLog(LL_NOTICE,
+                      "Failover occurred in migration source. Update importing "
+                      "source for slot %d to node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s.",
+                      slot, sender->name, sender->human_nodename, sender->shard_id);
+            server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot] = sender;
+        } else {
+            /* If the sender is from a different shard, it must be a result
+             * of deliberate operator actions. We should clear the importing
+             * state to conform to the operator's will. */
+            serverLog(LL_NOTICE, "Slot %d is no longer being imported from node %.40s (%s) in shard %.40s.",
+                      slot, server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot]->name,
+                      server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot]->human_nodename,
+                      server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot]->shard_id);
+            server.cluster->importing_slots_from[slot] = NULL;
+        }
+        updated = 1;
+    }
+
+    return updated;
+}
